In [19]:
import re
def startsWithDate(s):
    pattern='\[([0-2][0-9]|(3)[0-1])\/(((0)[1-9]|(1)[0-2]))\/(\d{2}|\d{4}), ((\d|(1)[0-2])\:([0-5][0-9])\:([0-5][0-9]) ([A|P][M])\])'
    result = re.match(pattern, s)
    if result:
        return True
    return False
In [20]:
def getDTAM(line):
    date=line.split(']')[0].split('[')[1].split(',')[0]
    time=line.split(']')[0].split('[')[1].split(',')[1].strip()
    if len(time)==10:
        time='0'+time
   
    if len(line.split(']')[1].split(':'))>1:
        author=line.split(']')[1].split(':')[0].strip()
        if len(line.split(']')[1].split(':'))>2:
            s=':'
            msg=s.join(line.split(']')[1].split(':')[1:])
        else:
            msg=line.split(']')[1].split(':')[1].strip()
    else:
        author=None
        msg=line.split(']')[1].split(':')[0].strip()
    return date,convertTo24(time).strip(),author,msg
In [21]:
def convertTo24(str1):  
    if str1[-2:] == "AM" and str1[:2] == "12": 
        return "00" + str1[2:-6] 
    
    elif str1[-2:] == "AM": 
        return str1[:-6] 
    
    elif str1[-2:] == "PM" and str1[:2] == "12": 
        return str1[:-6] 
    
    else:
        return str(int(str1[:2]) + 12) + str1[2:5]

parsedData = [] 

### INPUT FILE along with the path where it it located
with open(r"D:\\DataScience\\In\\Chat Analysis\\WhatsApp Chat - MITRA - 1 ASD Awareness\\WhatsApp Chat - MITRA - 1 ASD Awareness.txt","r",encoding="utf8") as f:

    f=f.readlines()
    messageBuffer = [] 
    date, time, author = None, None, None 
    for line in f:
        line=line.lstrip()
        count3=count3+1
        if len(line)>0:
            count6=count6+1
            if line[1]=='[':
                count5=count5+1
                line=line[1:]
            if startsWithDate(line):
                if count1==0:
                    line11=line
                line22=line
                print('T',line)
                count1=count1+1
                if len(messageBuffer) > 0: 
                    parsedData.append([date, time, author, ' '.join(messageBuffer)]) 
                messageBuffer.clear() 
                date, time, author, message = getDTAM(line) 
                if author == None:
                    count7=count7+1
                messageBuffer.append(message) 
            else:
                print('F',line)
                count2=count2+1
                messageBuffer.append(line) 
        else:
            print('B',line)
            count4=count4+1

T [14/06/19, 7:28:57 AM] +919866181757: Parents, This is a package to answer all your questions. Read it please.

B 
F 1. Why do many kids with autism Avoid eye contact ?

B 
F Different reasons, There is a difference between kids who actively avoid eye contact and kids who havent learned how to use eye contact during communication. For active avoiders, there is a sensory component where it is unpleasant for them to make direct eye to eye contact. One of the core deficits for individuals with autism is difficulty coordinating verbal and non-verbal means of communication. For example, while speaking to someone, a child may forget to make eye contact (which makes it difficult to know to whom the verbalization is directed). In addition, individuals with autism do not find communicative meaning in others eyes like the rest of us. Thus, they are not drawn to others eyes as information sources. Because of difficulty attaching meaning to the facial cues of caregivers and peers which relates to the childs social-communication skills.

B 
F 2. Why do many kids with autism . . . Cover their eyes/face/ears with their hands ?

B 
F This could relate to many things, such as the child covering their face as a way to block out too much sensory stimuli, to self-regulate, or to express feeling scared/anxious. Many children with autism have auditory sensitivities to specific sounds, such as a fire engine, baby crying, or toilet flushing. Covering their ears is one way to lessen the auditory input. Children with autism are often hyper-sensitive to auditory stimuli. Thus, sounds that are tolerable to us may be very loud and uncomfortable for them. Covering ears can often become a learned behavior and may be linked to anxiety as a child becomes fearful of potential unpleasant noises.

B 
F 3. Why do many kids with autism . . . Startle easily

B 
F The child may have difficulty anticipating everyday events, and filtering irrelevant social and environmental stimuli. When children startle easily, the result is frequently a fight or flight response.

F It may be sensitivity to their environments. A sound that we could tolerate may be startling to someone who is more sensitive to auditory input than others.

B 
F 4. Why do many kids with autism . . .Echo/repeat words/phrases

B 
F One of the primary communication deficits in autism is the tendency to echo or repeat words or phrases that are heard in ones environment. Because the brains language center has difficulty coming up with language on its own, it copies what it hears from the world around it and uses it in place of original words and sentences of its own. Its sort of like a Rolodex of phrases that the person pulls from at any given time in the day.

F Repeating words, or echolalia, is a common learning style for children with autism. Children with autism often learn language in chunks rather than creatively word by word. In addition, repeating words and phrases often serves a communicative purpose such as saying yes or helping with processing of information. Echolalia may relate to the child with autism having difficulty using more complex and spontaneous language. Echolalia can be a developmental phase and working alongside a SLP is very helpful to identify intervention strategies. As children develop more language, they may repeat phrases (e.g., from a movie) as a social initiation, or may learn to ask the same questions during conversation which helps make the interaction more predictable.

B 
F 5. Why do many kids with autism . . .Not talk at all

B 
F Talking or expressive language development requires understanding and use of symbols. Words, after all, are simply symbols for things, actions, and concepts. Sometimes children with autism lack or have significant delays in that ability. Children with difficulty with symbolic representation often have difficulty with understanding of language and use of other communication systems (e.g. sign language, Picture Exchange Communication System). Sometimes, children demonstrate the ability to understand language but have difficulty putting sounds together to form words. This can be a result of a motor speech disorder such as apraxia of speech. Its difficult to know why some children with autism do not talk or express themselves verbally. If possible, accessing alternative methods of communication, such as using gestures, pictures, typing, or a voice-output device is an important part of their social development.

B 
F 6. Why do many kids with autism . . .Walk on their toes

B 
F Toe-walking may be a learned habit (many toddlers walk on their toes), or may relate to motor coordination challenges, a tight Achilles tendon, or a sensory processing difference. Toe-walking is also seen with other neurological or developmental disorders, such as cerebral palsy. Children with autism often present with stereotyped motor movements, one of which may be walking on their tip-toes. Others hypothesize that walking on toes reduces over stimulation in the feet that can occur as a result of walking on the entire foot.

B 
F 7. Why do many kids with autism . . .Flap their hands

B 
F Children with autism tend to have repetitive motor behaviors such as waving or flapping their hands. This arm and hand motion may be accompanied with other motor mannerisms, such as jumping or head turning. Repetitive motor mannerisms, such as flapping hands (but also tensing parts of their body, jumping or dancing) are often linked to strong emotions (such as excitement or frustration). We see similar behavior in babies who eventually grow out of the behavior. These may also be self-soothing behaviors and/or attempts at regulating when what is perceived as overwhelming upset/excitement/boredom/anxiety is present.

B 
F 8. Why do many kids with autism . . .Like to spin and jump

B 
F Spinning and jumping are also examples of repetitive motor behaviors. When a child is spinning or jumping he/she is activating the vestibular system. The child may seek vestibular stimulation as a means to elicit feel good sensations and/or also to positively affect his/her arousal. In other words, many children with autism seek sensory information or experiences from the environment (due to feeling under-stimulated). They may also use spinning and jumping as a way of regulating themselves (i.e.: when they are stressed, anxious, or overwhelmed). Spinning and jumping can help one feel regulated and grounded.

B 
F 9. Why do many kids with autism . . .Have difficulty sitting still

B 
F The child may have sensory-motor challenges, or may have difficulty with attending behaviors. It is not uncommon for individuals with autism to present with hyperactivity and fidgety behavior. This is related to an executive functioning deficit that leads to difficulty regulating and planning behaviors and resisting impulses.

B 
F 10. Why do many kids with autism . . .Fixate on certain things (such as little things  tiny photo on a big page of a book or wheel of a big toy car)

B 
F When we think about it developmentally, children look at objects that are visually pleasing  such as rotating objects (fans, wheels, pinwheels). Fixating on certain things could also relate to visual processing, such as seeing the components of objects rather than the whole object, or perhaps the child has difficulty expanding play with toys and engages in repetitive play. Individuals with autism tend to have brains that think about things over and over. They may fixate on things that they find enjoyable or may get stuck trying to finish a task or game. A brain affected by autism tends to be more rigid and black and white. So it is hard to be flexible with a number of interests and ways of thinking about things.

B 
F 11. Why do many kids with autism . . .Stare into space

B 
F Some children dont realize they are staring  but may be tuning out what is overwhelming them or daydreaming about preferred interests. Individuals with autism are often very detail-oriented. Thus, they may notice details in the environment that we do not, and may get fixated on those details (thus, blocking all else out of their attention span and appearing to be spaced out).

B 
F 13. Why do many kids with autism . ..Have trouble with transitions

B 
F This relates to the way a brain affected by autism works  being less flexible than other brains. When it is fixated on something that it finds enjoyable, it has a hard time flexing to allow for new tasks or information to come in. It needs time and many reminders to switch to a new topic. 

F -------------------------------------------------------------------------------

F Hope this may help those of us who love someone with autism to describe and explain our kids behavior and allow others to understand them better. So DO NOT USE any treatments or diets to fix these. It's a different brain with different abilities. Thank you for understanding.

B 
F Dear Parents, Autism is a diagnosis, but it isn't a destiny or end or karma or the complicated technicalities from various groups and professionals. Let us join together and make the tears of sadness TO become tears of joy in our families. Yes, autism can be treated. The therapy is love, affection and trust.

B 
F Understanding the child is the golden key to unlock Autism.

B 
F We as parents should take this step and become a teacher, doctor, therapist, volunteer, friend and real parents for our child. Listen to all stories, methods, approaches. Contact APH or talk to other support groups for any questions or concerns. One more time, Autism does not have any discrimination. It strikes in South America, North America, Europe, Asia, Middle east and African countries. Autism effecting all people regardless of race, religion, cultures, rich and poor. You believe in GOD or do not believe in GOD. No matter what, it is a severe crisis in this planet. As research advances, as of now no known reason and no known cure for Autism. As parents, we are all in a long drawn war on Autism along with the support of friends, relatives, family members, doctors, teachers and autism families who is in the same situation. More families are joining Autism Parents Hub and with all your support we can improve the chances of children living happily with their abilities. Our goal is to provide support, help and inspire families who is facing difficult situations and challenges. Our weapons are help, support, education, awareness and positive approach. Do not lose hope. The skills and developmental milestones may or may not come with medicines, diet and moving kids to hostels or institutes etc. But the progress will surely come only with parents help, love and support. Our children are looking for HELP not for the treatments and therapies. They stepped in your family and looking at you for help. Just help. Only help and THE HELP. You are best parents for your child. Do not complain on children about their responses and behaviors.

B 
F Do not CONFUSE WITH WORDS LIKE HYPER ACTIVE, SENSORY, HYPER SENSITIVE etc. Knowing, loving, working and playing with a child makes all the differences in the happiness and well-being of the child. Bottom line is OUR CHILD. We believed parents can show him a way for the child into this world. No matter how severe the autism may be, our children can do progress. Early detection and intervention, therapies and positive approach can lead to good progress. To be able to live with autism and to make continuous progress day after day, we believe the parents should be the main teacher for their children.

B 
F We have seen parents who is treating this as a disease. The ignorance level about autism is very high.

B 
F APH will show the path and encourage that knowing, loving, working and playing with a child makes all the difference in the happiness and well-being of the child.

B 
F Autism may loom large, but it's secondary.

F No one can predict or should limit the future for any child with an autism diagnosis.

F Support the child abilities, rather than focusing on the weaknesses. 

F Were parents just like you. We understand the pain, confusion, fear, anger, and the other emotions that accompany an autism diagnosis.

F No matter how severe the autism may be, our children can do progress.

F Early detection and intervention, therapies and positive approach can lead to good progress.

B 
F Thank you and All the best.

T [15/06/19, 12:29:47 PM] +919866181757: 1. Set up a room or a place for home based therapy.

F 2. Buy Interactive books (books with more pictures and less content)

F 3. Take pictures of: 

F Child, family members, house, with in the house, outside the house, around the house, Stores, Petrol bunk/Gas station, Malls, Road, Sky, Clouds, Rain, Sun, Moon, Trees, leaves, Water, Fire, Dirty, Wet, Danger, Doctor, Police, Fire fighter, Teacher, School, Therapist, Family friends, Zoo, Haircut, Park, Play area, street, Money, Swimming pool, Baby, Boy, Girl, Time, Phone, Clock, Poisons, Theater, Traffic, Night, Day time, Bedroom, bathroom, Kitchen, Dress(pants, underpants, shirt...), Toys, Body parts, family members pictures, Emotions, Games, Alphabets, Numbers, Vegetables, Fruits, Vehicles, Animals, Birds, Shapes, Food, Breakfast items, Lunch items, Dinner items, Drinks, Snacks, appliances, Actions and Action words...etc.

B 
F Prepare four sets of pictures: 

F Use as Flash Cards

F Prepare charts and paste it on all the walls in your house. (charts)

F Save as back up

F Save as Pictures in your PC to show your child as many times as you can.

B 
F 4. Take/Create a video of all the material discussed in step 3. (Use dubbing or back ground voice (male and female) for each picture)

B 
F 5. Take pictures of child's or siblings or parents daily activities: 1. Child sleeping 2. Child Brushing teeth 3. Child washing face 4. Child's bath 5. Child activities 6. Child play 7. Child eating breakfast, snacks... 8. Child drinking water, juice...9. Child crying 10, Child's other activities like bike riding, swimming and all the daily needs.

B 
F 6. Take/Create a video of all the things discussed in step 5. (Use dubbing or back ground voice for each activities)

B 
F 7. Set up music therapy at home with children songs, rhymes etc...

B 
F 8. Prepare positive, negative re-inforcers AND prepare/implement cause-effect methods. (method to teach: You do this - you will get this)

B 
F 9. Set up a mirror to increase imitation skills in children. The best places for placing mirror...1. Bathroom 2. Therapy room 3. Dining room 4. Bedroom 5. Living room 6. Play room and most important a hand mirror to check the emotions right away. 

B 
F 10. Prepare audio files of:

F All the letter sounds, vowel sounds

F Child name

F Mom, Dad, Siblings, Family members

F Body parts, family members pictures, Emotions, Games, Alphabets, Numbers, Vegetables, Fruits, Vehicles, Animals, Birds, Shapes, Food, Breakfast items, Lunch items, Dinner items, Drinks, Snacks.

F All interested toy names, game names, activity names

F All the other words used in daily activities

F Run these audio files in any player (But child should not reach the player). The sound should be somewhere in the background. Run each files multiple times everyday. Try to be interactive to show the function or object in sync with the sound.

B 
F 11. Prepare a plan for teaching. (Fine Motor, Visual Motor, Oral Motor, Self Care, Sensory, Motor Planning, Gross Motor, Speech, Occupational, Social and Educational)

B 
F 11. Subjects for any child to become functional:

F 1. Occupational-Fine Motor

F 2. Speech/Book Reading/Tracing/Alphabets/Colors

F 3. Pretending/Imagination/Guessing/Find

F 4. Problem Solving/Puzzles/Memory Games

F 5. Gross Motor

F 6. Group play

F 7. Imitation

F 8. Actions - Body Parts

F 9. Friends/Family

F 10. Outside Behavior

F 11. Individual Play

F 12. Attention/Focus

F 13. Videos/Video Games/Internet/Computer

F 14. Sensory Play

F 15. Emotions/Feelings

F 16. Going out/Fun/Activities

F 17. Social Stories

F 18. Opposites

F 19. Environment

F 20. Decision making/Self Help

B 
F 11. Buy puzzles, interactive books, Interactive toys, Balls (basket ball, soccer ball, tennis ball, Soft balls, Plastic (all the colors)), balloons, Big Lego's, Pretending toys, Toy -  cars, trucks, musical instruments, magnets, top, stickers, play dough, bus, workbench, Stacking cups, train, phone, popping toys, animal toys, airplane, boat etc etc...

B 
F 12. Take the kid to all the places when ever and where ever possible. Do not keep the child at home all the time. (please). If any one say something, please respond "My kid is a slow learner, he is kinda tired. We are working and helping him". If they ask too many questions, ask the persons phone number and address or ignore them.

B 
F 13. Evaluate for every 1 month.

B 
F 14. Do not try any exploiting treatments for the child.

B 
F 15. CREATE RULES AT HOME.

B 
F 16. Steps need to be taken:

F 1. Talk to teachers/therapists about your concerns.

F 2. Discuss education plan for your child with therapist.

F 3. What kind of services are provided at School/Therapy center/Home ?

F 4. Autism Parents Hub will join with you and let us pool all the resources and work as a team.

F 17. Occupational Therapy (OT) is a health care profession that helps individuals with disabilities achieve their maximum level of independence in all areas of daily living, including work, play, self care and school. Occupational therapists work in a variety of treatment settings including hospitals, nursing homes, outpatient clinics and schools, to name a few. The information in this website is focused on OT services for preschool and school aged children.

B 
F Web sites for better learning: The key in finding the best resource depends on the skill you are trying to address, ease-of-use and functionality.

B 
F Here is the list of sites and apps and need to be introduced for the child one by one that has proven to be especially useful in both educating and entertaining kids with autism.

F 19. Please take child to all the social places. (parks, street, family friends, theater, rides, restaurant etc...)

B 
F 20. Senses: Please help your child to see all things, touch all things, smell all things, listen all sounds, taste all foods. (depends on limitations). This should be done everyday.

B 
F 21. Teach Swimming, Basketball, Cycle riding, Ball catch and throw, Skating, Music, rock climbing, martial arts and all the activities....

B 
F 22. Parallel Talk: Show Your Child What You Mean, Video modelling and keep talking along with gestures

B 
F 23. Do not lose hope. Please review your health, be happy and healthy. We are all one family.

T [15/06/19, 8:16:57 PM] +918800065000: Dear all, namaste

F My name is Rajni Singh and I am a special educator

F Just wanted to share a few things with one and all

F Much before being a therapist, I am a mother, I feel the same fears, same insecurities that all mums might be feeling when it comes to the well being and future of their kids

F Perhaps that fear was what kept me going with my kiddo I was told he wouldn't achieve much as he had quite significant behaviour issues,anyway, long story short, I experimented and failed and again experimented and so the journey continued.

F Today my 16yr old has cleared 10th standard with 72.8% and has chosen commerce stream and has successfully secured a seat in Father Agnel Junior College

F Being an autism parent is a journey...and every journey is different but the key as I feel, is to look inwards and not just rely on outside support

F Blessed are people like all the above mentioned experts and the admin of the group Sowjus, who are trying to bring help to the doorstep of all those who need it but the fact remains that we as mothers need to wake up to the fact that all of outside support is a complement, not suppliment, we need to take things in our hands and proactively learn to find ways that work for our kid, then all outside support will have compunded benefit, else, it really wouldn't help much

F As a thank you note to the universe for the amount of progress my son showed over the years , I started a you tube channel to be of value to other mothers.i paste the link to the same here for all mums to access. There are 80+ videos on various aspects of autism created primarily with the intention of creating an empowered and aware generation of parents, so we can do full justice to our autistic population

F Sorry for the long post dear readers

F Hope you find answers to what he seeking in some of the videos. Pls subscribe this is a free of cost service

T [16/06/19, 1:11:18 PM] +918800065000: Initiating speech is a matter requiring a lot of  motivation for a child ,so bring some super cool stuff(super cool according to kid, not you) means light n sound toys(please buy cheap ones cos u will need the by the dozens, it's surprising how soon they get bored or simply how they reject the toys, so don't spend huge deal on fisher price toys, just pick up random stuff sold on crossroads, some whistles, some tops that emit light, some LED balloons etc etc, then use them as manipulators, show him the toy once, keep aside, then ask him to say a particular word, even if he attprs, give the you ,but only for a few seconds then ask him to say another word, so on and so forth.

F Now, the words u choose for him to speak should also not be random words, he may totally not be interested in those, so see what all he is interested in at home, even if j find it silly, click a pic and take a print, start with 20such picks, paste in a copy or drawing file, keep it simple no decorations,very dont  want to distract the kid now place 4 pics on 4 corners so he doesn't get confused then first u say the name

F Ex, he is fascinated with garden pipe, so you say "pipe " and click pic and take print n post in copy/drawing file , now u get your manipulators(toys) by your side, now say to kid while finger pointing,  "pipe" then expect the kid to say "pipe" try, even if the kid can produce one sound or tries to give out a sound hugely praise clap etc etc raise noise, in a nutshell and give one light n sound toy but for not more than 10 seconds then take it back and show book again.

T [16/06/19, 1:12:55 PM] +918800065000: It is very important to remember the FREQUENCY INTENSITY DURATION PRINCIPLE: do the same 20 words, don't keep changing the words, do at least thrice a day, do without too much distraction around, phone ringing TV on etc

F So do this religiously for 10 days, u will see he begins to say the words, then u can add more words

T [17/06/19, 5:21:29 PM] +919866181757: Pinching, hitting, kicking, slapping:

B 
F Many of us know children with ASD might have difficulty with communication. Children with the given condition might not process or filter information about the expressions, sounds, words, thoughts, emotions, responses and feelings. So this often leads frustration and use different inappropriate methods of communicating feelings, getting attention, or protecting a territory.

B 
F However pinching, hitting, kicking, slapping is not an acceptable behavior in children, and it definitely wont fly as they grow up, so you need to nip it in the bud now, before it becomes a real problem.

B 
F How do you stop your child from these behaviors ?

B 
F You will first want to determine the cause of your childs actions.  If you dont know what is causing him to act out then you wont be able to effectively address the bad behavior.  Whether your child is hitting siblings, kids at school, or even himself, you need to know what triggers the attacks.  Is he upset about other children invading his space (getting too close, taking his toys, etc.)?  Or is he frustrated by an inability to communicate thoughts and feelings?  Maybe hes using self-abuse as a method of focusing or drowning out other sensory input.  If you cant figure it out on your own, you may want to see a professional who specializes in autism or behavioral analysis.

B 
F How to help your child.?

B 
F Once you have established the cause of your childs behavior, one method of dealing with it is to enact consequences. If you find that your child is hitting a sibling (this generally occurs during disputes over toys), then you must teach him the consequences of his actions just as you would any other child. Because children are often unable form a correlation between the pain they feel when they are hit and the pain they are inflicting on others through hitting, it will do no good to appeal to their sympathies or allow the other child to reciprocate as an example. Instead you may simply have to train them through cause and effect methods. 

B 
F So if your kids are fighting over a toy, take the toy away for a period of time. Or if the child is hitting other children for attention, put him in a time out. It may take awhile, but eventually he will learn that hitting equals consequences. When he has finished the time out, have him apologize so that you know he understands what he did wrong.

B 
F If cause and effect does not garner the desired results, you may want to switch tactics by implementing a rewards system. Try teaching your child an alternative to hitting others when he feels strong emotions. For example, use a designated pillow for hitting in place of a sibling so that he can act out his frustration without hurting anyone. Or teach him to hug instead of hitting (if he us able and willing to do so) so that he receives positive attention instead of negative. If he cannot form these associations, simply teach him to go to his own space, away from others, rather than hitting or acting out. This will at least keep him from hurting other children. Then encourage him when he utilizes his substitute by offering positive attention, praise, or other rewards.

B 
F Pinching, hitting, kicking, slapping - (Possible reasons)

B 
F frustration at not being able to communicate

F difficulty waiting for something, because of difficulty with concept of time and abstract thinking

F an unfamiliar person

F a change in routine

F over-sensitivity to noise, crowds, smells, touch, sight (see our information sheet The sensory world of the autism spectrum)

F under-sensitivity  seeking out sensory input from pinching or slapping

F feeling unwell, tired, hungry, thirsty, uncomfortable

F not wanting to do something.

B 
F Suggested strategies:

F use the Picture Exchange Communication System (PECS) and/or visual supports to help with communication and show your child the sequence of events and routine for the day

F prepare for meeting unfamiliar people by showing photographs of them and introducing them in small stages. Tell your child when they will see them, using visual support

F prepare for any changes in routine

F use ear defenders to block out noise and sunglasses to reduce light, and reduce strong smells, replacing them with smells that your child prefers

F create opportunities for sensory stimulation, eg pinching play-dough, clapping hands, singing a clapping song/rhyme, kicking a football or punch bag

F reward your child for doing something they dont want to do, straight after the desirable behaviour

F say in a calm, monotone voice, without showing emotion: (Childs name) hands down/feet down. No pinching, slapping, kicking and then redirect them.

B 
F Spitting

B 
F Possible reasons:

B 
F enjoys the reaction from an adult or another child around them

F is looking for attention/interaction

F has difficulty swallowing and/or may be producing too much saliva

F likes to play with the saliva and enjoys the way it feels

F uses the behavior to avoid doing something.

F Suggested strategies:

B 
F take your child to the GP and/or dentist to rule out any medical reasons

F avoid making eye contact with your child

F play this behavior down as much as possible

F limit verbal communication

F wipe away the saliva as soon as it happens

F do not give your child attention

F redirect them to a more appropriate activity

F provide alternative sensory activities, eg water play, finger painting, etc

F give your child lots of positive attention for doing a more appropriate activity

F give them a sweet or something to suck to keep their mouth busy

F make sure they understand what is expected and redirect them to a visual timetable.

B 
F Consistency, Language, Rewards, Relaxation:

B 
F Consistency

B 
F Although these kinds of behaviors can be extremely challenging, it is really important to try and keep as calm as possible so that your child is unable to feed off your reaction. It is also important to be consistent in your approach and for the other adults around to use the same consistent approach, so that your child does not get mixed messages and can be really clear about what is expected.

B 
F Language

B 
F By reducing language, your child is less likely to feel overloaded by information and more likely to be able to process what you say. Children with an ASD are often strong visual learners and can have difficulties with short-term memory. It can be very effective to back up what you are saying to your child with visual supports, which consolidate what you say and to help your child really understand the information.

B 
F Rewards

B 
F Using rewards and motivators can help to persuade your child finish a task that they do not want to do, or to encourage a particular behavior. Even if the behavior or task is very short, eg one minute, if it is followed by lots of praise and a reward, the child learns what behavior is acceptable. But if the undesirable behavior is met with a lack of attention and redirection, it is likely to stop.

B 
F Relaxation

B 
F It can be helpful to build in opportunities for children (and parents!) to relax each day. You can do this by, for example, looking at bubble lamps, smelling essential oils, listening to music, massages, swinging on a swing or whatever you can find that seems to help your child relax. Challenging behavior can often be diffused by an activity that releases energy or pent-up anger or anxiety. This might be punching a punch bag, bouncing on a trampoline or running around the garden, which you can make into a chase game.

T [18/06/19, 11:04:43 AM] +919445573753: How far is the language delay!? Let's say if he makes 1 or few true words, his language age is of 1 year of age. So he's delayed by 1 year. So it would take atleast 9 months of intensive stimulation at home to get his language age appropriate. Hence I suggest, to work with child at home intensively for next 9 months. Pre/ play isn't necessary much, moreover when you put him in 4 hrs of school, you won't have time to work with him at home. Presently acquiring language is more important than academic skills. Number of hours of productive parent-child interaction is more important than number of speech therapy sessions. Hope this helps..

T [18/06/19, 11:10:57 AM] +919445573753: Irrespective of reasons for delay in language, usage of (scientific / published) language stimulation methods & techniques for management are going to be same anywhere you go. The pattern in which the language parameters progress in the child would be same the typical Development pattern. So plan & work, monitor progress regularly.

T [20/06/19, 8:20:15 PM] +1(501)2569270: @All

F Welcome to MITRA.

F Thank you for taking time and joining MITRA.

F Mission of MITRA(MOM) is to provide useful information to parents of kids with some extra needs. 

F I have taken lot of efforts in collaborating with 

F Well Experienced professionals to provide useful information to parents.

B 
F I would like to thank each and every one of them to proactively join with me in MITRA to help parents 

F In providing information that will be beneficial to the kids.

B 
F I have also collaborated with ADMINs of other groups to promote awareness. I would like to thank them for positively collaborating with me.

B 
F MITRA group will be a platform to discuss useful information about therapies and techniques that are research backed and scientific and evidence based. We will be discussing about OT,PT,ABA,Speech and other relevant therapies. It is also encouraged to discuss about music and other relevant scientifically backed information.

B 
F However MITRA will not encourage discussions on Ayurveda, Homeopathy, Bio- medicine or any other Syrups or medications that magically treat ASD related disorders. 

F I request Parents and Professionals to please keep the posts and discussions relevant to scientific and evidence backed Information.

F If you want to discuss on these MITRA probably wont be the right platform for you. 

B 
F We will be adding professionals from time to time who will be helpful in providing useful information in MITRA for parents.

B 
F Please post your queries and professionals in the team will provide information when they are free. Please keep in mind that they will be taking time off from their busy schedules to answer any queries. Please be patient. Any information shared in MITRA is for parents awareness only. 

B 
F Once again welcome all and thank you so much for Joining MITRA. 

B 
F #Admin.

T [21/06/19, 7:57:55 AM] +919873986285: 7 Benefits of Yoga for Kids with autism. 

B 
F 

B 
F 1. Yoga develops motor skills. Kids with autism frequently experience delayed motor development, which can be improved as yoga tones muscles, enhances balance and stability, and develops body awareness and coordination. As motor skills develop, children have a greater sense of their physical self in space and in relation to others, and can improve their gait and stability. This leads to

B 
F 2. Yoga improves confidence and social skills. Poor coordination often yields low self-esteem as kids may be singled out or teased for not moving or behaving like other children, or not excelling in sports and outdoor activities. By learning self-control and self-calming techniques through yoga, they are likely to grow confidence in interacting with other children and refine their social skills. Learning to work together in a yoga class and playing with partner poses can also increase confidence within group settings.

B 
F 3. Yoga provides sensory integration. Children with autism often suffer from a highly sensitive nervous system and are easily over stimulated by bright lights, new textures, loud noises, strong tastes and smells. Yogas natural setting of dim lights, soft music, smooth mats, and inside voices creates a comforting environment largely protected from unknown or aggressive stimuli in which calming down becomes enjoyable. Yogas physical poses allow nervous energy to be released from the body in a controlled manner, also leading to a calming sensation. Less stimulation means less uncontrollable behavior, outbursts and repetitive nervous movements  which is further enhanced by

B 
F 4. Yoga provides coping techniques to both kids and parents. Whether teaching the child breathing techniques for self-calming, talking the class through a guided visualization the child can use when getting anxious, or sharing flashcards of the days poses with parents to use at home, yoga provides an awesome toolbox to parents and siblings. It is a transportable practice that both parents and kids can draw from for a lifetime and share a meaningful home activity.

B 
F 5. Yoga facilitates self-awareness. Yoga is particularly instrumental in helping kids with autism learn self-regulation. By becoming aware of their bodies and aware of their breathing, yoga provides them with the ability to cope when they start to feel anxious or upset. Many 'Yoga for Autism' classes teach yoga poses or breathing techniques specifically intended to help children contend with their escalating emotions. Since these children are visually oriented, savvy instructors add a visual element so that the child has a colored picture of each pose near his or her mat. Often, classes incorporate other experiences known to benefit a child on the autism spectrum, such as massage, music, dance, rhymes and stories

B 
F 6. Yoga engages the emotional brain. We all know that yoga is far from purely physical, and this combination of movement, music, breath work and story telling activates the brains emotional region. This encourages children to develop awareness of their emotions and those of others, as well as keeps their attention in the class. Music is another powerful tool that the yoga instructor can share with parents to use at home to recreate the environment of a yoga class.

B 
F 7. Yoga is orderly and consistent. Ideally, the class will be scheduled at the same time and same day of the week, with the students mats in the same layout, in the same room, with the same instructor(s). In my experience, there was one instructor per student, with the pairing the same week after week to impart a sense of trust and steadiness. This element of order is very important for a child and communicates stability  a state much preferred to being unexpected and thus out of control. Students may also enjoy learning yoga sequences, such as modified sun salutations, that are performed in the same order at every class. The class should have an opening and closing routine or practice  singing, tuning in, etc.  that further supports the students need for order .

B 
F *Happy International Yoga Day to All.*

F Dear parents , all our autistic/ adhd kids do have lots of social and behavioral issues in terms of emotions, peer relations, conduct problems , hyperactivity and social interactions. Me with my  team  at gigglesclinics have come with a questionnaire on social and behavioural analysis which will give u complete report on behavioural and social issues of the child and accordingly positive parenting techniques.

T [23/06/19, 5:13:02 AM] +1(813)4542873: Hello moms .... In another group a mom asked how I started working on speech and language when my son first got diagnosed. No way I am an expert and I need a lot of guidance myself. I am sharing what I wrote on the other grp. May help someone.

T [23/06/19, 5:13:27 AM] +1(813)4542873: Hi Neha ... Speech and Language is still challenge for us  I remember Kabir making sounds when he was 2 but not call me mom. Articulation was ok but no functional language. He would pull my hand to. Show me what he wanted. As soon as he got diagnosed we started speech therapy and OT. But he wasn't talking. Slowly ecolhalia developed. So we started showing him pictures with written words and sounded it out for him. I remember labling everything in my house. I started taking him to every object and showing him the written name. I would say it first and made him repeat. Slowly he learned. At the same time we started using iPad. He enjoyed touching the pictures that made sound. So labeling apps really helped. 

F Slowly he started requesting what he needed. Only one word for .... Water, swing, etc later we made him say I want/can I have. Lots and lots of modeling. Then we moved on to actions .... Play, read, drive etc. And at he same time taught him funtion of objects ex book is for reading, ball is for playing etc. So he learned to say I want to read.

T [23/06/19, 5:13:28 AM] +1(813)4542873: We sing a lot. Nursery rhymes, bollywood songs etc. Its simple and there is no guessing involved so it encorages him to use his voice. Whenever he is swimming vocally .... Whole family starts to sing his favorite rhymes.

T [23/06/19, 5:13:29 AM] +1(813)4542873: Stimming I mean

T [23/06/19, 5:13:29 AM] +1(813)4542873: We had a speech therapist working with us who gave us goals to keep practicing.

T [23/06/19, 5:13:30 AM] +1(813)4542873: His receptive language has come so far now. And we are working on expressive as well.

T [23/06/19, 5:13:31 AM] +1(813)4542873: Reading came easier than talking. So at times I write the response he suppose to give. Thats how he learned to respond to "Hello how are you".

T [23/06/19, 5:13:32 AM] +1(813)4542873: Much of it is rote but as comprehension is getting better , I see his speech improving as well.

T [24/06/19, 7:07:41 AM] +919866181757: Parents, Every parent ask APH - Where should we begin ?

B 
F The beginning - Sleep patterns. (Better sleep  - Better focus, Less tantrums, better behavior, better health for both child and parents).

B 
F - Without nailing this down -  No use of any behavior intervention.

B 
F Good sleep habits is an entry door for any behavioral interventions.

B 
F To do list: 

B 
F Increase child's physical activity level during the day (trampoline, walks, playground, etc.).

F Restrict naps during the day.

F Evaluate the bedroom for environmental noises

F Use a consistent bedtime routine.

F Avoid watching TV because it can interfere with sleep.

F Avoid extending the time for bedtime.

F Avoid drinks and foods like soft drinks, juices and chocolate before bed time.

B 
F Sleep Program:

B 
F Please try this for 3 months consistently. See the change.

B 
F - Make sure child has more physical activity.

F - Less or No day naps

F - No television and computers for one to two hours before bedtime

F - Rough play should be eliminated for one to two hours before bedtime

F - Dinner before 7-30 PM

F - 7-30 PM to 8 PM : Massage (Head and body)

F - 8:00 PM - Bath

F - Music On - Only soft music

F - Quiet activities such as drawing, looking at books, or playing with puzzles or construction sets are more suitable activities for a period before bed.

B 
F - 9:00 - Bed time begins. Lights off and Continue music.

F After the child is in bed, a back-rub may also be soothing. Again, be sure to start with the neck and go down to the base of the spine. Use slow, rhythmic strokes; when one hand is at the base on the spine, start at the back of the neck with the other hand.

B 
F Once the patterns are established, you will be able to reclaim a large part of your evening for yourselves.

B 
F *****When child wakes, don't turn on lights, talk, etc. Keep everything neutral and silent. See if the child need something like water or potty then continue the same pattern. *****

B 
F All the best.

T [24/06/19, 4:02:01 PM] +919445573753: To improve his conversation & narration skills, improving his length of sentences. Length of sentences would increase with increasing vocabulary. To improve vocabulary, 

F - introduce lots of verbs (hoping he has mastered nouns & it's categories)

F - work on Questions & Description at same time.

F - now work on pragmatic skills / social Communication

F - now work on modelling (don't expect him to say); describing picture, scenes, narrate stories, events, sequence & schedule.

F - no create situation where let him try conversation & narration.

T [24/06/19, 10:20:25 PM] +919866181757: Dear Parents, As long as you are in the technical trap(words) of:

B 
F - Hyperactivity

F - Behaviors

F - Eye contact

F - Sitting tolerance

F - Speech

F - Sensory 

F - Autism

B 
F You are trapped for your life and you will never see your child's abilities or strengths or happiness. Please do not use these or think about these if you really want to help your child. Think outside the box. Please do not become cash boxes for doctors and professionals.

B 
F Functional development is the key. You are best parents for your child. Do not complaint on children about their responses and behaviors. No matter what, our children are smart, but they couldn't tell us what they knew. Its going to be okay if you help at the right time, right place and with the right support.

B 
F Do not forget the basic "Every kid is different". No doctor or professional is better than a parent. Do not focus much on academics first. The first skill for any child is to function and communicate. Understanding the child is the golden key to unlock Autism. Knowing, loving, working and playing with a child makes all the differences in the happiness and well-being of the child.

T [26/06/19, 2:02:55 PM] +917022569499: Hi All.  I will write how my daughter became socially interactive here. 

B 
F My daughter used to get scared when new person come near to her. When we moved to gated community of independendent houses, I found lot of children here. As usual she used to get scared when kids come near. I started talking to the children by holding my daughter in my hands. Children became friendly to me. They started coming to my home to play with toys. I used to play with the children and my daughter used to see and she used to smile.

F Later I made her to sit in my lap and started playing with neighbor kids. Slowly she started interacting with them.

B 
B 
F I used to play with only 2 or 3 children at a time. If more children are around her, she gets confused to whom she has to look at. 

B 
F Now my daughter wants to play with the kids. As she is not able to walk now, I will make her stand with my support when children are playing and she enjoys it.

B 
F I started interacting with kids parents by holding my daughter in my hands. She used to observe them and her fear is reduced. Now she is giving hands to neighbours to hold her.

T [28/06/19, 5:30:33 AM] +1(501)2569270: @Dear All members,

F The mission of MITRA is to help mothers struggling in their daily lives trying to deal with the challenges of ASD diagnosis in their

F children. 

B 
F It is not for commercial advertisements, guarantees, challenges to one another,

F authenticity verifications or voicing the clash of opinions - personal or professional.

B 
F ASD does not have geographical boundaries and can impact the lives of parent in suburban New York city to a small village.

B 
F When a mother in remote village who is a member of this group reads the conversations, we at MITRA want her to feel that she is getting her questions answered, doubts cleared, a ray of hope visible and light at the end of a long dark tunnel.

B 
F We want the mother to know what to do, how to address her child's needs and make educated decisions.

B 
F We at MITRA while acknowledging the their expertise, education and experience, plead that the professionals and educators announce their list of therapies, services and locations and deal with the commercial element when the parents contacts them privately. Thank you.

B 
F The reason for this endeavor is that I personally know some mothers in small villages who cannot commute or relocate to cities because of economic reasons. This is a small effort to help them in what ever way we can . I hope you all Understand.

T [28/06/19, 9:15:58 AM] +918008719793: Hai all

F Sleep disturbances are categorically observed to be

F 1.inconsistent sleep.

F 2.waking up early and waking frequently.

F 3.restlessnes or poor quality.

F 4.difficulty falling sleep.

F What I observed or the closest theories to explain this are

F 1.increased sensitivity to outside stimuli,such as touch and sound (may b opening washroom doors,changing bedsheets,pillow covers,etc).

F 2.hormone melatonin-to make hormone melatonin body requires amino acids (trytophan), these are found to be high or low.

F 3.has got to do with social cues (circadian rhythms)

F Finally if we understand this then I think it becomes easy to get th child to sleep

T [28/06/19, 9:23:53 AM] +918008719793: Hai

T [29/06/19, 6:17:58 AM] +918008719793: Dear ma'am

F There are three things which I can understand

F 1.cross eye look

F I guess you're asking about peripheral vision.

F If so 

F Then usually children on spectrum can't focus in midline because they can't appreciate or vision in midline will be blurred. In other words it's called astigmatism.

F Cylindrical lens can help to overcome this.

F 2. Spinning in rounds

F Could be because of visual and vestibular hyposensitivities

F Provide the child with strong visual stimuli and get a swing made at home and encourage her to engage in that.

F neutral warmth will also help her

F 3.tactile issues

F Make her play with corn flour and messy play...which includes some water colours and mud at home.

T [29/06/19, 8:36:53 AM] +919445573753: Parents need to understand Myths, Misconceptions & Reality of using Augmentative Alternative Communication Systems. (AAC)

F Myth 1: AAC is a last resort in speech-language intervention.

F Myth 2: AAC hinders or stops further speech development.

F Myth 3: Children must have a certain set of skills to be able to benefit from AAC. 

F Myth 4: Speech-generating AAC devices are only for children with intact cognition.

F Myth 5: Children have to be a certain age to be able to benefit from AAC.

F Myth 6: There is a representational hierarchy of symbols from objects to written words (traditional

F orthography).

B 
F I have taken lot of efforts in collaborating with Well Experienced professionals.

B 
F I would like to thank each of these professionals who joined  me in MITRA to help parents in providing information that will be beneficial to children on the spectrum.

B 
F MITRA group will be a platform to discuss useful information about therapies and techniques that are research backed and scientific and evidence based. We will be discussing about OT,PT,ABA,Speech and other relevant therapies. It is also encouraged to discuss about music and other relevant scientifically backed information.

B 
F However MITRA will not encourage discussions on Ayurveda,Homeopathy, 

F Bio- medicine or any other Syrups or medications that are rumored to magically treat ASD related disorders. If you want to discuss on these MITRA probably wont be the right platform for you.

B 
F I request Parents and Professionals to please keep the posts and discussions relevant to scientific and evidence backed Information.

F . 

F We will be making continuous efforts to add more professionals to the group.

B 
F Please feel free to post your queries and professionals in the team will provide information when they are free. Please keep in mind that they will be taking time off from their busy schedules to answer any queries. Please be patient. Also please be respectful and kind to each other and avoid any criticisms that are unwarranted.Any information shared in this group is for parents awareness only. 

B 
F Once again welcome all and thank you so much for Joining MITRA.

F ===> build self esteem.

F ===> reduces anxiety.

F ===> socialization.

F ===> be more independent.

F ===> improve learning process.

F ===> get ready for the next activity without anxiety.

F ===> reduce stress.

F ===> be more independent.

F ===> teach in small steps (break big tasks into small steps).

T [01/07/19, 12:59:12 PM] +919966632169: Hi all I am dr.madhusudhan reddy and dentist (oral pathologists) by profession. My daughter 3.4 years with SPD is on OT, speech therapy, GFCF diet since 1 year. Since then there is a gradual improvement and at present her sensory issues have reduced alot and speech is not attained yet. Regarding GFCF diet can be followed by every one. But usefulness of it should be assessed and continued if positive results are shown. As they are growing children they need good nutrition for their proper growth and development. So when your stopping certain type of food especially milk their dietary calcium is cut off and their bone health is hampered. Before starting GFCF diet please take suggestions from your pediatrician and you also can meet dietitians and discuss about the gfcf diet and ask them to give a diet chart which can be tailor made according to your child which can give a good nutrition to your child and help in proper growth and development. You also can supplement the child with multivitamin and calcium only under the supervision of your pediatrician. To certain extent GFCF diet has helped my daughter. But only following GFCF doesn't help much. OT, ABA, ST combinedly can do miracles.

T [02/07/19, 5:00:24 AM] +1(813)4542873: Seeing the Big Picture (Central Coherence)

B 
F The whole is greater than the sum of the parts.  The invisible relationships between the parts (how they relate together) provide more meaning to the collection of parts alone.  Central coherence is the brains ability to see the invisible relationships between the parts, which give an overall meaning to the whole.  The brains of neurotypical (NT) people have a natural ability to seek out overall meaning when looking at an array of details.  We seek overall meaning immediately when viewing detail.  We immediately search for invisible relationships that provide meaning to the details.  When looking at something, our brains scan for a few important details to grasp the big picture.  From the first impression, we then tend to use the overall picture to provide the backdrop for defining the individual details.  Our brains seek out "meaning" first, then detail second.  We tend to think from "general to specific."  This is what happens when we immediately see a smiling face out of two dots with a half moon under it.  Or, when we quickly skim written material, missing misspelled words, and reading the meaning without paying attention to the individual words.   This also allows us to read the invisible context that provides meaning to how we interpret what people are saying and doing.  We often infer, meaning quickly when faced with a few details.  From there, we go on to interpret all other details by the initial interpretation we assume.

B 
F For many people on the spectrum, their brains tend to work the opposite.  Their brains focus on the detail and not the overall picture.  They struggle to see the invisible relationships between the parts and have to search for overall meaning by piecing together the details.  They are more acutely aware of the fine detail and do not immediately get pulled into seeing the relationships (hidden meaning) between the parts.  They first scan the many details and then put them together to form the overall meaning.  They tend to think "specific to general" rather than "general to specific."  They see the parts literally, with less bias, and then piece the parts together to form the overall picture.  

B 
F This difference in processing provides the person with autism many unique strengths as well as weaknesses.  They have a much more concise, concrete, literal interpretation of what they perceive.  They are very strong detailed thinkers, can perceive detail with minimal bias, and pick out imperfections among the detail.   Unlike the neurotypical brain, autistics often perceive all of the details at once with minimal filtering:  however, piecing them together might take time.   This leads some to have photographic memories, perfect pitch, and profound memory for details and facts.  They also can acutely perceive the physical relationships (physical patterns) between the details.  They often are superior in perceiving sensory patterns (e.g., visual and auditory patterns) that we may not attend to.    For tasks requiring extreme acuity to detail (e.g. engineering) their processing is very strong.  Also, there fine attention to sensory patterns can be valuable in arts and music.  However, as we will see later, when it comes to interacting and relating, this weak ability to rapidly interpret the overall picture (central coherence) can leave them struggling.

B 
F Qualities of Weak Central Coherence 

B 
F 1. Problems Seeing the Big Picture

B 
F a. Good with detail, not global perception.

F b. Difficulty seeing invisible relationships between the parts.

F c. For us, the whole is more than the sum of its parts.  For ASD, the whole is the sum of its parts.

B 
F 2. Concrete Thinkers

B 
F a. Difficulty reading context. 

F b. Takes things literally.

F c. Doesnt quite get it! Doesnt see the big picture.

B 
F 3. Misinterprets & Misjudges

B 
F a. Troubles extracting the overall meaning of events. 

F b. Difficulty with multiple meanings.

F c. Cannot read between the lines.

F d. Often misinterprets and then acts out of context.

B 
F It is very important to keep in mind the difficulty people on the spectrum have in understanding the invisible cues, relationships, and context that provide meaning to much of what we interpret.  This is why we cannot assume, provide information very literally and clarify then verify understanding.  Do not assume!

B 
F These two processing differences represent great strengths at opposite ends, but also strong conflict when they clash in daily living.   The unbiased, literal perception for detailed is so valuable in sciences, arts, and technology.   This processing strength is so valuable to the development of humankinds future medical, scientific, and technological development.  However, when living daily in our neurotypical driven society, the limited ability to read the invisible social context, infer perspectives and intentions of others, and vague social rules that come with inferring the invisible relationships often renders them confused and clashing with the expectations of others.  We have to appreciate the strengths that each processing style offers and learn to accommodate the conflicts that arise when integrating them both together. 

B 
F This series on cognitive issues in autism can be found in the blue book, Autism Discussion Page on the Core Challenges in Autism.

B 
F http://www.amazon.com/s/ref=nb_sb_noss_2?url=search-alias%3Daps&field-keywords=Bill+Nason

T [02/07/19, 7:10:21 PM] +918008719793: Parents need to understand Myths, Misconceptions & Reality of using Augmentative Alternative Communication Systems. (AAC)

F Myth 1: AAC is a last resort in speech-language intervention.

F Myth 2: AAC hinders or stops further speech development.

F Myth 3: Children must have a certain set of skills to be able to benefit from AAC. 

F Myth 4: Speech-generating AAC devices are only for children with intact cognition.

F Myth 5: Children have to be a certain age to be able to benefit from AAC.

F Myth 6: There is a representational hierarchy of symbols from objects to written words (traditional

F orthography).

T [02/07/19, 7:11:15 PM] +918008719793: Sleep

T [02/07/19, 7:11:37 PM] +918008719793: Sleep

T [02/07/19, 7:11:55 PM] +918008719793: Hai all

F Sleep disturbances are categorically observed to be

F 1.inconsistent sleep.

F 2.waking up early and waking frequently.

F 3.restlessnes or poor quality.

F 4.difficulty falling sleep.

F What I observed or the closest theories to explain this are

F 1.increased sensitivity to outside stimuli,such as touch and sound (may b opening washroom doors,changing bedsheets,pillow covers,etc).

F 2.hormone melatonin-to make hormone melatonin body requires amino acids (trytophan), these are found to be high or low.

F 3.has got to do with social cues (circadian rhythms)

F Finally if we understand this then I think it becomes easy to get th child to sleep

T [03/07/19, 5:11:23 PM] +919654156623: Replacement behaviours techniques are the ways by which u modify child wrong/ difficult into more constructive and appropriate behaviuor by providing him that extra sensory input. These behaviours occur particularly due to sensory overload.

F For eg : bitting : he needs extra sensory input in mouth : so provide him with some crunchy food .

F Hitting/ scratching: he needs sensory input in fingers: give him squeeze balls in his hands.

F Head banging : vestibular sensory input : teach him side ways nodding along with some light music this way he can learn and can maintain eye contact. These are just some examples.

## This cell will tanke more time when comapred to other cells based on the amount of data, at max it executed for 2-4 minutes for me
dict1={}
for s in cat1:
    dict1[s]=[]
dict2={}
for s in cat2:
    dict2[s]=[]
dict3={}
for s in cat3:
    dict3[s]=[]
dict4={}
for s in cat4:
    dict4[s]=[]
dict5={}
for s in cat5:
    dict5[s]=[]
dict6={}
for s in cat6:
    dict6[s]=[]

for line in chatdf['Message']:
    line1=[]
    line1.append(line)
    df=pd.DataFrame(line1,columns=['msg'])
    
    for s in cat1:
        media_messages_df= df['msg'].str.lower().str.contains(s)
        if media_messages_df.bool():
            dict1[s].append(df['msg'])
            break
            
    for s in cat2:
        media_messages_df= df['msg'].str.lower().str.contains(s)
        if media_messages_df.bool():
            dict2[s].append(df['msg'])
            break
            
    for s in cat3:
        media_messages_df= df['msg'].str.lower().str.contains(s)
        if media_messages_df.bool():
            dict3[s].append(df['msg'])
            break
            
    for s in cat4:
        media_messages_df= df['msg'].str.lower().str.contains(s)
        if media_messages_df.bool():
            dict4[s].append(df['msg'])
            break
            
    for s in cat5:
        media_messages_df= df['msg'].str.lower().str.contains(s)
        if media_messages_df.bool():
            dict5[s].append(df['msg'])
            break    
            
    for s in cat6:
        media_messages_df= df['msg'].str.lower().str.contains(s)
        if media_messages_df.bool():
            dict6[s].append(df['msg'])
            break
